Jamison Brereton

110
R╠еbhus
Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
9 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 5 and 9
The R╠еbhus are originally mortal craftsmen who achieved immortality because of a series of marvelous deeds. This hymn begins in the ritual here-and-now, where the R╠еbhus, already immortal, are offered their share of the sacrifice by the poet-sacri ficer, who speaks in the 1st person. The story of their achievement is then begun in verse 2, with the R╠еbhus depicted as itinerant skilled workers, rather like the poet and his comrades (thus perhaps holding out the hope that immortality will come to them as well). The particular feats they accomplished are then recounted, with special emphasis on their turning Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs single cup into four (vss. 3, 5), the oth ers hurriedly covered in verse 8, interspersed with pleas for their favor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬс╣Ъbhus, the rite formerly celebrated by me is again repeated, and the melodious hymn is recited in your praise; in this ceremony, the Soma is sufficient for all the gods; drink of it to your utmost content when offered on the fire.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

My (ritual) work has been stretched out, and it is being stretched out again. My sweetest insight is being recited for a hymn.

Right here is the sea (of soma) belonging to the All Gods. Satiate
yourselves together on the (soma) prepared with the sv─Бh─Б-cry, o R╠еbhus.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out, the mention of the All Gods (vi┼Ыv├бdevya-) marks the ritual reference as the Third Pressing, which is dedicated to the All Gods and in which the с╣Ъbhus have their share. This suggests that the repeated stretching in p─Бda a need not refer only to the periodic nature of Vedic sacrifice over the ritual year, but also perhaps to the repeated rites of the Soma pressing day. Since the theme of the тАЬleftoverтАЭ is prominent in the Third Pressing (see Jamison 1996: 129-32), тАЬbeing stretched out againтАЭ fits this context.

Griffith

THE holy work I wrought before is wrought again: my sweetest hymn is sung to celebrate your praise.
Here, O ye Rbhus, is this sea for all the Gods: sate you with Soma offered with the hallowing word.

English translation:

тАЬWhen, с╣Ъbhus, you who are amongst my ancestors, yet immature (in wisdom), but desirous of enjoying (the Soma libations), retired to the forest to perform (penance), then, sons of Sudhanvan, throught he plural nitude of your completed (devotions), you came to the (sacrificial) hall of the worshipper Savit─Б.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъbhurvibhv─Б v─Бja iti sudhanvana ─Бс╣Еgirasasya trayaс╕е putr─Бс╕е babh┼лvuс╕е (Nirukta 11.16): Sudhanvan, father of the с╣Ъbhus, was a descendant of Aс╣Еgiras; so is Kutsa;

Jamison Brereton

When, facing front, you shrewd ones went forth in search of your daily bread, kind of like my pals,
o sons of Sudhanvan, after your fill of roaming you came to the house of Savitar the pious.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, the wandering с╣Ъbhus seem here to be compared to the poet and his ilk, tramp craftsmen in search of skilled work – as Geldner already suggests. (For more on itinerant priests and poets, esp. the Pr─Бtaritvan, see Jamison 1996: 184-89.) In p─Бda b ├бp─Бk─Бс╕е is universally interpreted as тАШwestwardтАЩ, derived from ├бp─Б├▒c-, contrasted with immediately following pr─Б╠Б├▒caс╕е тАШfacing eastwardтАЩ. So, e.g., Geldner тАЬAls ihr тАж westw├дrts, ostw├дrts weiter zoget.тАЭ Although the direction words frequently co-occur, one might expect the stem formations here to be parallel, that is, using a form of ├бp─Б├▒c- rather than a derivative. Cf., e.g., pr─Б╠Бg ├бp─Бg ├║d─Бk (III.53.11, VIII.4.1=VIII.65.1). Moreover, the с╣ЪbhusтАЩ journey seems to be purposeful and directed, given the two pr├б forms (тАж pr├б тАж a├нtana тАж pr─Б╠Б├▒caс╕е) and the fact that they reach a goal. I take ├бp─Бka- instead as a privative form of p─Б╠Бka- тАШcallow, simple(ton)тАЩ, hence тАШnot simple; clever, shrewdтАЩ; cf. ├бm┼лra- тАШnot stupid, no foolтАЩ to m┼лr├б- тАШstupidтАЩ.

The tone of the locution m├бma k├й cid ─Бp├бyaс╕е is somewhat hard to read; it is reminiscent of V.52.12 t├й me k├й cin n├б t─Бy├бvaс╕е. The effect seems to be approximative – тАЬsome kind of X,тАЭ тАЬmore or less like XтАЭ – and slightly slangy. The referent of the m├бma is the 1st ps. speaker of vs. 1, contra Renou, who takes the phrase as the direct speech of (one of?) the с╣Ъbhus.

Griffith

When, seeking your enjoyment onward from afar, ye, certain of my kinsmen, wandered on your way,
Sons of Sudhanvan, after your long journeying, ye came unto the home of liberal Savitar.

Geldner

Als ihr Unterhalt suchend westw├дrts, ostw├дrts weiter zoget als gewisse Bekannte von mir, da gelanget ihr S├╢hne des Sudhanvan nach vielem Wandern in das Haus des opferspenden Savitri.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThen Savit─Б bestowed upon you immortality, when you came to him, who is not to be concealed, and representd (your desire) to partake of the libations; and that ladle for the sacrificial viands which the Asura had formed single, you made fourfold.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who is not to be concealed: In the previous hymn, Savit─Б (from su, to offer oblations) perhaps refers to the presenter of oblations; in this hymn, the sun is alluded to

Jamison Brereton

Then Savitar impelled you to immortality when you went to make Agohya heed.
This very beaker, the drinking vessel of the lord [=Tvaс╣гс╣нar]тАФthough it was single, you made it fourfold.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─Б╠Бsuvat тАШimpelledтАЩ is of course a pun on Savitar, its subject.

The final p─Бda is parallel to 2a: тАж pr├б y├бd ich├бnta a├нtana / тАж y├бc chravay├бnta a├нtana, each with a pres. part. combined with the main verb a├нtana.

What exactly is happening in 3d is unclear, since Agohya is a shadowy figure in с╣Ъbhu mythology. In с╣Ъbhu hymns they sleep in his house (I.161.11, IV.33.7); the most similar passage to ours is I.161.13, where the Rbhus ╠е after their sleep ask him ├бgohya k├б id├бс╣Г no ab┼лbudhat тАЬO Agohya, who has awakened us here/now?тАЭ In our passage the mirror-image action seems to be depicted – they’re making him heed, that is, waking him up. I do not know what to do with this observation, however.

Griffith

Savitar therefore gave you immortality, because ye came proclaiming him whom naught can hide;
And this the drinking-chalice of the Asura, which till that time was one, ye made to be fourfold.

Geldner

Da beschied euch Savitri die Unsterblichkeit, als ihr den Agohya anrufend kamet. Ihr habt sogar jenen Becher, das Trinkgef├д├Я des Asura, der einzig war, vervierfacht.

Grassmann

Darum verlieh euch Savitar Unsterblichkeit, weil ihm, den ewig hellen rufend, ihr erschient, Den Becher auch, aus welchem trinkt der ew’ge Gott, den einen habt ihr in vier Becher umgeformt.

Elizarenkova

тАШ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╡реЛрдврд╛рд░реЛ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдорд░реНрддрд╛рд╕рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рдореГрддрддреНрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╢рд┐рд░реЗ рд╕реМрдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛ рдЛрднрд╡рдГ рд╕реВрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реВрд░рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЗ рд╕рдордкреГрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдзреАрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рд░реНрдЛрднреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рднреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЬ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реБрдзрдиреНрд╡рди рдЖрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рд╕реНрдп рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛ рдмрднреВрд╡реБрдГ’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. резрез. резрем) рдЗрддрд┐ рее рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реАред тАШрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд▓реГ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддреМ ред рд╕реНрдирд╛рддреНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рджрдпрд╢реНрдЪ ’ ( рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рен. рез. рекреп ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕реНрдп рдИрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рд╢рдореА ред тАШ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд▓реБрдХреН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рд╕реЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред рдЖрдирд╢реБрдГ ред тАШ рдЕрд╢реВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддреМ’ред рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдореИрдкрджрдореН ред тАШ рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреЗрд╢реНрдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрднреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рджреБрддреНрддрд░рд╕реНрдп рдиреБрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ ред рдЕрдкреГрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрдд ред’ рдкреГрдЪреА рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдХ ‘ред рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд▓рдЩреН рее

English translation:

тАЬAssociated with the priests, and quickly performing the holy rites, they, being yet mortals, acquired immortality and the son of Sudhanvan, the с╣Ъbhus, brilliant as the sun, became connected with the ceremonies (appropriated to the different season) of the year.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Toiling with labor, with surpassing skill, the cantors, though they were mortal, reached immortality.
The sons of Sudhanvan, the R╠еbhus, who have the sun as their eye, in a year became infused with insights.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand why the с╣Ъbhus are called v─Бgh├бt- here, since this term is ordinarily used of ritual officiants (see comm. ad I.3.5) and the с╣Ъbhus only indirectly participate in ritual. Geldner tr. тАЬdie fahrende (?) S├дnger,тАЭ but he provides no support for the itinerant part of the tr.

As Geldner points out, s┼л╠Бra-cakс╣гas- is characteristic of gods; in I.89.7 it is used almost as a definition of such. So it may well here be an ancillary indication that the с╣Ъbhus achieved divine status.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рд╕реМрдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛рдГ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╕реВрд░рдЪрдХреНрд╖рд╕рдГ) рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЬрд┐рдирдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдмрд▓ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╣реИ (рд╡рд╛рдШрддрдГ) рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдХрд╣рдиреЗ, рд╕реБрдирдиреЗ (рдорд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд╕рдГ) рдорд░рдиреЗ рдФрд░ рдЬреАрдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдЛрднрд╡рдГ) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН рдЬрди (рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЗ) рд╡рд░реНрд╖ рдореЗрдВ (рдзреАрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд╛ (рд╕рдордкреГрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрдд) рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдз рд░рдЦрддреЗ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рдо рдХрд╛ рдврдЩреНрдЧ рд░рдЦрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рд╡реЗ (рддрд░рдгрд┐рддреНрд╡реЗрди) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реА) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╢рдореА) рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрд░рддреЗ (рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ) рд╣реБрдП (рдЕрдореГрддрддреНрд╡рдореН) рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рднрд╛рд╡ рдХреЛ (рдЖрдирд╢реБрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее рек рее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпреЗрдХ рдХреНрд╖рдг рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ-рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рд▓реЗрдХреЗ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрдд рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдХрд┐рдиреНрддреБ рдЖрд▓рд╕реА рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдХрднреА рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛ рд╕рдХрддреЗ рее рек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рд╕реМрдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реВрд░рдЪрдХреНрд╖рд╕реЛ рд╡рд╛рдШрддреЛ рдорд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд╕ рдЛрднрд╡рдГ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЗ рдзреАрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердпреБрдХреНрддреИрдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдВ рд╕рдордкреГрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдкреГрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рддрд░рдгрд┐рддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реА рд╢рдореА рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рдореГрддрддреНрд╡рдВ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рднрд╛рд╡рдорд╛рдирд╢реБрд░рд╢реНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее рек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

they who were crying in want at the praise-invocation, seeking highest fame among the immortals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

├║pastut─Б in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text is universally taken, flg. the Pp., as the nom. pl.

of the past part., ├║pastut─Бс╕е. I take it rather as the loc. sg. of ├║pastuti- тАШpraiseinvocationтАЩ. It doesnтАЩt make sense to me that, after having been praised, they would be тАЬcrying in wantтАЭ and seeking (further?) fame, whereas if they lack praise at the praise invocation, their seeking fame is understandable. Loc. sg. -─Б to -i-stems is found only interior in the p─Бda as here, but almost always before consonants.

However, AiG III.152 counts 9 occurrences before -u-/-┼л-, as here.

Geldner and Renou take upam├бm as the obj. of n─Б╠Бdham─Бn─Бс╕е, but that stem is never transitive (as Renou admits), and it appears in the preceding hymn (I.109.3) in clear intransitive usage. I take the adj. with ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е in d. It would also be possible to take it as an adverb: тАЬin utmost need.тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н construe it with the cup in b; this seems the least likely possibility, since the miraculous deed of the с╣Ъbhus is depicted only in the first hemistich, quite separately their quest for fame in the second.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo the leaders (of the sacrifice), dwelling in the firmament, we present, as with a ladle, the appointed clarified butter, and praise with knowledge those с╣Ъbhus, who, having equalled the velocityof the protector (of the universe, the sun), ascended to the region of heaven, through (the offerings) of (sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nс╣Ыbhyaс╕е = yaj├▒asya netс╣Ыbhyaс╕е; с╣Ыbhavo hi yaj├▒asya net─Бraс╕е: ’the с╣Ыbhus are the leaders of the sacrifice’; because of this position, they obtained immortality; the term is perhaps connected with antarikс╣гasya, to the chief of the firmament; с╣Ыbhus also identified with the solar rays (─Бdityara┼Ыmayo api с╣Ыbhava ucyanti: the с╣Ыbhus are, indeed, said to be the rays of the sun

Jamison Brereton

Let us pour an inspired thought with our know-how, like ghee with a ladle, for the men of the midspace.
Those who by their surpassing skill followed (the way) of the father of this one, the R╠еbhus mounted to their prize, the realm of heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The conceptual basis for the common trope of тАЬpouring prayersтАЭ is made clear here by the simile тАЬlike ghee with a ladle.тАЭ Because of its lack of accent asya cannot modify pit├║с╕е and it should have a referent already present in the discourse. The referent is generally taken as the cup of 5 and its father as Tvaс╣гс╣нar. I do not have anything better to offer.

GeldnerтАЩs tr. of c seems very loose and somewhat puzzling: тАЬтАж die die P├╝nktlichkeit seines Vaters erreichten …тАЭ He seems to be taking taraс╣Зitv─Б╠Бas neut. pl.

rather than instr. sg. (like taraс╣Зitv├йna in 4a) and imposing a meaning тАЬerreichtenтАЭ on sa┼Ыcir├й that stretches the semantics of that stem. Renou makes a good case for the instr.

interpretation, and supplies an acc. тАЬ(lтАЩexemple)тАЭ that allows the usual тАШfollowтАЩ sense for the verb. My tr. is similar.

v─Б╠Бja- in d is a low-key pun on the name of one of the с╣Ъbhus.

Griffith

As oil in ladles, we through knowledge will present unto the Heroes of the firmament our hymn,–
The Rbhus who came near with this great Father’s speed, and rose to heaven’s high sphere to eat the strengthening food.

Geldner

Wir wollen den Herrn des Luftreiches kundig eine Dichtung als Opfer bringen wie Schmalz mit dem L├╢ffel. Die Ribhu┬┤s, die die P├╝nktlichkeit seines Vaters erreichten, die haben als Lohn den Himmelsraum erklommen.

Grassmann

Des Luftraums M├дnnern wollen kundig ein Gebet wir giessend weihen wie mit L├╢ffeln Butterseim, Die Ribhu’s, die mit ihres Vaters Siegerkraft sein Gut gewannen, stiegen auf zum Himmelsraum.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe most excellent с╣Ъbhu is in strength our defender; с╣Ъbhu, through gifts of food and of wealth, is our asylum; may he bestow them upon us, Gods, through your protection; may we, upon a favourable occasion, overcome the hosts of those who offer no libations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(One) R╠еbhu is for us a newer Indra by his power; (another) R╠еbhu is a good one by his goods, a giver by his prizes.
With the help of you, o gods, on a favorable day may we stand up to the battle thrusts of those who donтАЩt press soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In my interpr. the individuation of the с╣Ъbhus continues in ab, though not with their usual names.

Note the switch in number between the opening of 6d с╣Ыbh├бvo v─Б╠Бjam (pl. - sg.) and that of 7b с╣Ыbh├║r v─Б╠Бjebhiс╕е (sg. - pl.).

In b the instr. pls. v─Б╠Бjebhir v├бsubhiс╕е are ordinarily taken as proper names and instr. of accompaniment. I instead take them as defining the quality for which the с╣Ъbhu gets designated тАШgood oneтАЩ and тАШgiverтАЩ. My tr. also assumes a chiastic structure in v─Б╠Бjebhir v├бsubhiс╕е v├бsur dad├нс╕е, with the first instr. construed with the last nom. sg.

and the middle two terms belonging together.

The analysis of pс╣Ыtsut├н- is debated (see, e.g., Renou EVP XIII.108; AiG II.2.640 ┬з473a╬▓A.; III.73, ┬з29b; II.1 Nachtr. 67). On the one hand, it appears to be a compound consisting of the root noun pс╣Ы╠Бt- and a primary -ti-stem, probably to тИЪs┼л тАШimpelтАЩ (with shortening, like s├║-с╣гuti to the other root тИЪs┼л тАШgive birthтАЩ). On the other, since the root noun pс╣Ы╠Бt- is only attested in the loc. pl. pс╣Ыts├║ (though the root is also found in the derivatives pс╣Ы╠Бtan─Б-, etc.), pс╣Ыtsut├н- appears to be a secondary -t├н- stem anomalously built to a case form. This seems to be the current standard view.

However, it seems entirely possible to me that we are dealing with a haplology of

*pс╣Ыtsu-sut├н- (or -s┼лt├н-), and my tr. reflects this analysis.

Griffith

Rbhu to us is Indra freshest in his might, Rbhu with powers and wealth is giver of rich gifts.
Gods, through your favour may we on the happy day quell the attacks of those who pour no offerings forth.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬс╣Ъbhus, you covered the cow with a hide, and reunited themother with the calf; sons of Sudhanvan, leaders (of sacrifice), through your good works you rendered your aged parents young.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: a с╣Ыс╣гi, whose cow had died, leaving a calf prayed to the с╣Ыbhus for assistance, on which, they formed a living cow, and covered it with the skin of the dead one, from which the calf imagined it to be its own mother

Jamison Brereton

O R╠еbhus, you carved out a cow from a hide; you sent the mother to join with her calf again.
O sons of Sudhanvan, superior men, with your skillful work you made your two elderly parents young.

Griffith

Out of a skin, O Rbhus, once ye formed a cow, and brought the mother close unto her calf again.
Sons of Sudhanvan, Heroes, with surpassing skill ye made your aged Parents youthful as before.

Geldner

Aus dem Fell formtet ihr Ribhu┬┤s eine Kuh und lie├Яet die Mutter wieder mit dem Kalb zusammen. Ihr S├╢hne des Sudhanvan, durch eure Kunstfertigkeit machtet ihr die greisen Eltern jung.

Grassmann

Ihr habt, o Ribhu’s, aus dem Fell die Kuh geformt, die Mutter habt ihr wieder mit dem Kalb vereint, Ihr habt mit Kunst, o Helden aus Sudhanvans Stamm, die altersschwachen Aeltern wieder jung gemacht.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдГ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд╛рдЬреЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдЬреИрд░рдиреНрдирд╛рджрд┐рд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реАрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ (рдирдГ) (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдЕрд╡рд┐рдбреНрдврд┐) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд▓реГрдзрд╛рддреЛрдГ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХрд┐ рд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ рдордзреНрдпрдореИрдХрд╡рдЪрдиреЗ рд╣реЗрд░реНрдзрд┐рдГ рд╖реНрдЯреБрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬрд╢реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдкрд┐ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГред (рдЛрднреБрдорд╛рдиреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛ рдЛрднрд╡реЛ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ (рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рдореН) рдЖрд╢реНрдЪрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЖ) (рджрд░реНрд╖рд┐) рджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджрд░рдВ рдХреБрд░реБред рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреГрдЩреН рдЖрджрд░ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рд▓реНрд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ рдордзреНрдпрдореИрдХрд╡рдЪрдиреЗ рд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрддрд┐ рддрд┐рдкрдГ рдкрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреНрдЧреБрдгрдГред (рд░рд╛рдзрдГ) рдзрдирдореНред рддрдиреНрдиреЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛ рдорд╛рдорд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдирд╣рд┐ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЛ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорддрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреЗрди рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬреЗрддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдиреЛрддреАрддрд┐ рее реп реердЕрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдордЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧреЛ рджрд╢реЛрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
